National Calendar Year-End Accounting

The Social Affairs Bureau Does Not Allow Flexibility

The Bean and Rice Trade Association and the Rice Milling Trade Association, citing the difficulty in complying with the national calendar year-end accounting at the end of May and September, have twice petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting a temporary change in the year-end accounting period. The Bureau has now issued a response rejecting the request. The Bureau's response is transcribed below: The petition has been noted. The revision of the national calendar accounting date and the phased completion were decided after soliciting the opinions of the business community and careful consideration. It has been approved by the National Government and promulgated throughout the country for unified compliance. It has also been implemented by the Shanghai Municipal Government's Announcement No. 107. Last year, the national calendar year-end was pressing, and merchants were not prepared to settle accounts, so a temporary extension was granted. However, starting from 1930, absolute compliance should be observed, and no excuses should be made. Upon inspection, the petition states that the year-end accounting coincides with the time when new goods are on the market and funds are needed to accumulate grain, resulting in tight capital turnover. Without rice on the market next year, and with financial stagnation leading to grain stagnation, farmers and rice dealers will suffer. It is argued that the national calendar year-end accounting method is extremely difficult to comply with. In fact, the harvest of agricultural products, according to the solar terms, means that the late rice is ripe at the latest around the Frost's Descent solar term, and the harvest is completed. There are still two months until the year-end accounting, and farmers have plenty of time to sell rice. Moreover, the accounting and New Year's holidays are at most half a month, and a short-term stoppage should not cause inconvenience. The argument that financial stagnation leads to grain stagnation is illogical. It is likely that the association is afraid of reform and has made this request. It should be known that the difference between the national calendar and the lunar calendar is only two solar terms, with leap years being an exception. Now, the government is promoting the national calendar, and the people should also eliminate the habit of complacency and strive to comply. There is no such thing as a trial run, let alone a question of political tutelage or constitutional government. The Bureau supervises and enforces compliance and will not allow the industry to be an exception. The request to set February 15, 1931, as the year-end closing date is difficult to approve. You are hereby notified. This response.

Shanghai Chinese Steamship Companies to Fully Resume Operations

Total Number of Chinese Steamships in Shanghai

Since the Central Government's suppression of the rebellion, Chinese steamship companies in Shanghai have suspended operations for two years. During this military period, foreign steamship companies have been very active in the Yangtze River and North-South Seas routes. Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Nissin, and Kawasaki have been competing fiercely. Now that the Central Government's suppression of the rebellion has come to an end, the chartering of merchant ships should also come to an end. Recently, the Transportation Department of the General Headquarters has returned eight chartered ships to various steamship companies, which were used to transport the triumphant army to Jiangxi and Anhui provinces. The chartering of ships will be completely over soon. From November onwards, the Chinese steamship companies in Shanghai that have been suspended for a long time are expected to fully resume operations. The preparations for resuming operations and expanding routes of Chinese steamship companies, as well as the current tonnage of all steamships in Shanghai, are detailed below. This is also a major opportunity for the continuation of Chinese shipping.

Establishment of the Zhongwei New Steamship Company

Regarding China's recovery of shipping rights, British shipping merchants in Shanghai have stated that if the tonnage of Chinese steamships can meet the needs of commercial transportation, foreign merchant ships will automatically abandon various routes in China. Now, Chinese shipping merchants Chen Shuntong and Zhang Shusheng, in order to develop the national shipping industry, have raised 400,000 yuan to organize a new steamship company called Zhongwei. First, 100,000 yuan was used to purchase a steamship named Taiping, with a capacity of 4,000 tons. The head office has been established on Sichuan Road and Fuzhou Road and has already started operations, dispatching ships to the Haizhou area. Next spring, it is planned to purchase another ship to operate on the North-South Seas ports.

Request for Relief for the Shipping Industry

Yu Qiaqing, the owner of the Sanbei Company in Shanghai, submitted a request to the Central Government, stating that Chinese steamships have suffered huge losses during the military period. Now that the war is over, various companies urgently need relief. In addition to organizing a shipping bank to issue 10 million yuan in shipping bonds, it is also requested that the General Headquarters provide a subsidy of 1,000 yuan per month for each chartered merchant ship to compensate for the losses of long-term suspension of operations and to cover the increased hidden losses of various ships. This request has already been submitted.

Survey of Chinese Steamships in Shanghai

There are still 18 Chinese steamships in Shanghai that are currently suspended. It is expected that all of them will be able to resume operations within a week. Various steamship companies in Shanghai are already planning to resume operations. The number of Chinese steamships in Shanghai is something that the commercial transport industry urgently wants to know. The details are as follows:

China Merchants Bureau Investigates Director Wang of Hankou

Director Wang Hao of Hankou Dismissed for Misconduct and Investigated

Deputy Chief of Accounting Section Deng Xieyang Dismissed

Li Yunliang Appointed as Director of Hankou Bureau

Since Mr. Li Zhonggong took over the China Merchants Bureau, he has been striving to rectify the accumulated malpractices of various branches and ships, which have been criticized by the society for a long time. Mr. Li is now starting to conduct a thorough investigation in preparation for rectification. Yesterday, it was learned that Wang Hao, the director of the Hankou Branch, had taken advantage of his position and engaged in private misconduct while serving as the secretary-general during Cai's tenure. Mr. Li was extremely angry and immediately ordered his dismissal and investigation. In addition, Deng Xieyang, the deputy chief of the accounting section, was also dismissed at the same time for being negligent in the same case. Li Yunliang, the deputy chief of the business [illegible] section, was appointed as the director of the Hankou Branch. A reporter from Xin Sheng News believes that this matter is of great importance to the future of the bureau's rectification. The details are as follows: Wang Hao is very stubborn. Since taking office as the director of the Hankou Branch in 1928, he has often neglected the orders of the head office. Zhao [illegible] repeatedly wanted to replace him but failed. During Cai's tenure, Wang also served as the secretary-general of the head office, which was a great overstepping of his authority. According to the branch regulations, if the annual income exceeds the quota, an extra bonus can be drawn for distribution to the branch staff. However, the distribution must be approved by the head office. Although Wang repeatedly requested the issuance of extra bonuses for the Hankou Branch in 1928 and 1929, Zhao approved only one month's double salary because the overall business of the head office was very sluggish and the Hankou Branch's overdraft in 1928 exceeded the quota by a huge amount, which should be deducted according to regulations. Therefore, the appropriation of the above bonus was not allowed. This case was delayed for two years. When Wang served as the secretary-general, he thought he could take the opportunity to seek approval and obtain tens of thousands of yuan. On the day before the current director Li Zhonggong took office, he hastily drafted a report without obtaining Cai's approval and ordered Deng Xieyang, the deputy chief of the accounting section, to transfer the money and cancel the registration, and also filled in the date and month on the original report and correspondence books to cover up the matter. The transfer voucher was filled in with the date of Li's assumption of office, which was September 13 (Saturday). Mr. Li performed the inauguration ceremony in the morning. In fact, the bureau staff had no time to work. The afternoon was the usual closing time (the bureau usually does not work on Saturday afternoons). No one was responsible, so Wang took advantage of the chaos to rob. Unexpectedly, this act of taking advantage of his position for private gain was reported, and Mr. Li ordered a strict investigation. After the evidence was confirmed, he ordered his dismissal and investigation yesterday.

Shanghai Waterworks Company Agrees to Prepare Balance Sheet

Reply to Taxpayers' Association Letter

The Shanghai Waterworks Company replied to the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association yesterday regarding the audit matter, stating: "In response to your association's letter of the 8th of this month, requesting that the company's profit and loss statement and balance sheet for January 1 to June 30, 1930, be submitted to your association's representatives for review, this company has already submitted for review by your association's representatives the 1930 expenditure statement and profit and loss statement prepared by this company based on the actual figures for the first half of this year. As for the accounts for the first half of this year, the company's chief accountant unfortunately passed away in February, and the successor took over for only one week, so it has not been fully prepared yet. Moreover, the company has only been settling accounts every six months in recent years for the reference of the directors and not for the review of the shareholders. Whether the semi-annual balance sheet should be prepared this year is still a question. However, if your association's representatives are determined to review the figures, this company will certainly do its best to prepare them immediately, but it may take three or four weeks to complete them." This reply is hereby given.

Labor Arbitration Ordinance Canceled

Future Disputes Can Be Handled by Law

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued an order to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "In order to comply with the order, the case concerns the Municipal Government's Order No. 6026, which includes the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's Order No. 1585 regarding the transmission of information. The case concerns the previous approval of the Anhui Provincial Government's Order No. 390 regarding whether the 'Measures for Handling Labor Disputes' can be interpreted and handled by referring to the 'Labor Dispute Handling Law' before its promulgation. The 'Labor Dispute Handling Law' is a special law, and labor dispute cases cannot be used by analogy. However, the 'Labor Arbitration Council Ordinance,' promulgated in August 1926, was originally established to resolve disputes between workers at that time. It is now being questioned whether it is still applicable. The Executive Yuan and the Judicial Yuan have been consulted for interpretation, and the Ministry has also first consulted the Anhui Provincial Government for reference. It has been replied that the content of the 'Labor Arbitration Council Ordinance' is largely incompatible with the current administrative system, and labor dispute cases can be handled by applying general laws. It seems that the ordinance can be explicitly abolished or amended and supplemented separately. The Executive Yuan has been consulted for review by the Legislative Yuan. Now, the Executive Yuan's Order No. 3483 states: 'The case concerns the notification of the matter. The Ministry has previously submitted that the content of the "Labor Arbitration Council Ordinance" is largely incompatible with the current administrative system, and labor dispute cases can be handled by applying general laws. If the ordinance should still be implemented as before, it should also be amended and supplemented separately with opinions and submitted for review and transmission to the Legislative Yuan.' A copy of the 'Labor Arbitration Council Ordinance,' promulgated on August 16, 1926, was submitted to the court. After reviewing the situation and copying the ordinance, it was transmitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. In response to the notice, the Legislative Yuan's Order No. 97 states: 'The case concerns the Executive Yuan's Order No. 187, based on the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's request to explicitly abolish the "Labor Arbitration Council Ordinance" or amend and supplement it separately, please review it.' At the 106th meeting of the court on August 23, 1930, it was decided to submit it to the Labor Law Drafting Committee for review. According to the review report, it was stated that: 'The members met on September 12 to discuss the matter together and agreed that the ordinance was originally established to resolve disputes between workers at that time. Now, disputes between workers are relatively less common than in previous years. If such disputes occur, administrative agencies can apply general laws to handle them as appropriate, and there is no need to establish separate ordinances. Moreover, the content of the ordinance is largely incompatible with the current situation. It seems that it can be submitted to the National Government for explicit abolition and need not be amended or supplemented.' It was requested to submit it to the General Assembly for a public decision. At the 110th meeting of the court on September 20, 1930, it was decided to adopt the review report. In addition to requesting the National Government to explicitly abolish the 'Labor Arbitration Council Ordinance,' the corresponding record was consulted for reference." This order was issued, and the Ministry was ordered to notify the chamber to follow the order and instruct all subordinate commercial organizations to be informed.

Important Cases Decided by the Food Committee

Discussing Issues of Maintaining Farmers' Economy and Sufficiency of People's Food

The Municipal Food Committee held its 19th regular meeting at the Social Affairs Bureau on the 18th. More than ten experts, committee members, and leaders of the rice industry attended the meeting. Committee member Feng Liutang proposed seven measures to maintain the farmers' economy and ensure the sufficiency of people's food. Committee member Zhu Yinong proposed levying a surtax on food imports. After joint discussion, it was decided that: (1) It is recommended to levy import taxes on major food grains to fund agricultural improvement and the Central Disaster Relief Fund; (2) It is requested that the Central Government issue an order to all provinces and cities to prepare statistics on the amount of rice and grain harvested in each place this year and the amount consumed in previous years within three months, so that the Central Government can establish a grain regulation policy and order all provinces and cities to comply; (3) All provinces, cities, and counties should uniformly restore warehouses starting this year and store three months' worth of grain according to the size of their population. If there is less, they must apply to the higher-level government for approval. The method of raising funds should be determined by each locality; (4) The import of Japanese rice should be investigated immediately to determine the amount already imported. It is requested that the Central Government promptly determine the method, and those that have not yet been shipped should be prohibited from importing; (5) Members of the Food Industry Committee of this committee should investigate the amount of harvest in various production areas. Those in Jiangsu and Zhejiang must report to the committee within two weeks, and those in Hunan and Jiangxi must report to the committee within four weeks for reference; (6) Those merchants and businessmen in this city who store more than 5,000 piculs of grain and operate in accordance with the city's regulations on public storage of rice and grain shall be commended by the government.

Social Affairs Bureau Strictly Prohibits Watered Rice

The bad habit of watering rice in the Southern Gang rice industry in this city undermines commercial ethics and harms the health of citizens. The Social Affairs Bureau has issued two announcements strictly prohibiting it and has sent personnel to secretly investigate at any time. It has been found that most places such as Wujiang Tongli in the Southern Gang have complied, but rice from Shengze is still watered. Yesterday, rice merchants Yan Xiaoquan and others were strictly ordered to investigate and report, and the bad habit of watering rice must be completely eradicated by the end of the year. If it is found after the deadline, the ships and goods will be confiscated to serve as a warning.

Petition to the Municipal Government from Chinese Property Owners Regarding Rent Collection

Rent Collection Should Be Limited to One Month

Pan Peide and others, Chinese property owners in this city, have submitted a petition to the Municipal Government regarding the collection of rents, stating that the total monthly rent income in the Chinese-administered area of this city is indeed one million yuan. As such, in the matter of raising funds for customs bonds through rent collection, please change the period from two months to one month to alleviate the difficulties faced by businesses. Upon investigation, your office has been ordered to raise one million yuan in short-term customs bonds for the 19th year of the Republic. A public notice has already been issued to collect two months' worth of rent. The property owners believe that the total rent income for two months in the Chinese-administered area of this city exceeds two million yuan, which is more than double the amount allocated by the central government. This is an unbearable burden. On the eighth of this month, they jointly submitted a petition to your office, requesting a flexible approach to collect only one million yuan, and to publicly announce the amount of rent received at any time to demonstrate transparency and alleviate the people's difficulties. The deadline is approaching, but no instructions have been received yet. The property owners are at a loss and do not know what to do. They believe that the total monthly rent income in the Chinese-administered area does indeed exceed one million yuan. They hereby request to prove this amount with the following facts: (1) In the 16th year of the Republic, two months' rent was collected in this city's Chinese-administered area as a patriotic donation, totaling approximately 2.5 million yuan. Old donation records are available for verification, which proves that the total monthly rent in the Chinese-administered area of this city should be around 1.25 million yuan. (2) Furthermore, the 17th-year business report published by the city's Finance Bureau states that the annual rent tax collected in this city is 1.3 million yuan. It is an undeniable fact that there are more residential properties than commercial properties in the Chinese-administered area of this city. If we assume that residential properties account for 60% and commercial properties account for 40%, then out of the 1.3 million yuan, 780,000 yuan is collected from residential properties and 520,000 yuan is collected from commercial properties. The rent tax rate for residential properties is calculated at 14% of the rent. The total annual rent income for commercial properties should be 3.7 million yuan. The total annual rent for residential and commercial properties is 11.5 million yuan, with a monthly average of 960,000 yuan. This is the bare minimum. (3) In fact, the total monthly rent income in this city is definitely more than 960,000 yuan. Although the rent tax in Zhabei is calculated at 100% of the rent amount, the rent tax in Hujiang is first reduced to 75% of the rent and then calculated at 10% or 14%. It is an undeniable fact that Zhabei is far more prosperous than Hujiang, so the total rent is less in Zhabei than in Hujiang. If we assume that Zhabei accounts for 40% and Hujiang accounts for 60%, then out of the 960,000 yuan in monthly rent, only 380,000 yuan belongs to Zhabei, and 580,000 yuan belongs to Hujiang. This 580,000 yuan is calculated based on the proportion of rent tax collected, and the actual rent in Hujiang is reduced by 25%. Therefore, we should add one-third of the original amount to the 580,000 yuan, which is 190,000 yuan, for a total of 770,000 yuan, which is the actual monthly rent collected in Hujiang. Adding the 380,000 yuan from Zhabei, the total monthly rent in the Chinese-administered area of the city is actually 1.15 million yuan. (4) Furthermore, according to the rules for collecting rent tax in this city, rent tax for charitable organizations and schools is usually exempted or reduced. However, this time, rent is collected across the board. Therefore, the actual monthly rent in this city is more than 1.15 million yuan. (5) The above calculations are based on the rent tax collected in the 17th year of the Republic. However, in recent years, the rent has increased considerably due to the reconstruction of old houses and the construction of new houses in the Chinese-administered area. Therefore, the current monthly rent is more than 1.15 million yuan. (6) It is said that your office exempts property owners with a monthly rent of less than three yuan from collecting rent. However, it can be said that there are very few property owners in this city with a monthly rent of less than three yuan. It is impossible to use this as an excuse to say that the monthly rent collected in this city is less than one million yuan. Based on the above facts, it can be said with certainty that the monthly rent in the Chinese-administered area of this city is more than one million yuan. Since your office has been ordered to raise customs bonds limited to one million yuan, collecting rent for one month is more than sufficient. Why collect rent for two months, exceeding the amount by more than double, causing many difficulties for property owners due to financial turnover issues? If you say that the amount that should be collected according to the above figures cannot be regarded as the actual amount collected, then your office is using a public notice approach, which is mandatory. With the credibility of your office, coupled with the assistance of the military and police to pay rent on behalf of tenants, the strength of your collection power is far greater than the usual rent collection situation of property owners. There is no reason why the monthly amount of more than one million yuan cannot be collected in full. The property owners have repeatedly considered that it is difficult to bear the burden of doubling the borrowing. For this reason, they respectfully request that your office quickly change the borrowing period to one month, so that the collection will stop as soon as the amount is met. The gratitude for your kindness will be boundless. This petition is respectfully submitted.

US Restrictions on Egg Yolk Imports

Foreign Trade to be Affected

City Chamber of Commerce Cables Ministry to Request Negotiations

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in Nanjing, stating: According to a letter from the Shanghai Egg Products Manufacturers Association on the 20th of October, the industry has long been shipping machine-made egg yolk (commonly known as "Flying Yellow") to Europe and the United States. Except for occasional cases where newly-established companies produced substandard products that rotted upon arrival overseas, resulting in rejection, there have been no restrictions. In recent years, the Americans have been meticulously planning to seize the profits from egg production from our country. They first vigorously advocated increasing taxes to seek to resist our products. When increasing taxes failed, they revised new regulations this year, limiting the acidity of imported Chinese Flying Yellow to five degrees. Any acidity exceeding this limit will be considered spoiled and rejected for import. The acidity of Flying Yellow is originally below this limit when it is freshly produced. However, the acidity increases with prolonged storage. Merchants sometimes store goods temporarily to wait for favorable prices when market prices are not suitable. This is a common commercial practice to seek speculative gains. If we are subject to this strict restriction, then once the goods are manufactured, they must be sold immediately, regardless of profit or loss. Perhaps, we would not even dare to start manufacturing without firm orders. Furthermore, the manufacture of this egg product is concentrated in egg-producing areas in the interior, and transactions occur in treaty ports open to both Chinese and foreigners. If there are unexpected delays during transportation at various stages, causing the acidity to exceed the limit, the goods will also be rejected. The bankruptcy of merchants will be imminent. The US restriction on acidity is a conspiracy to undermine our egg production industry. For this reason, we are forced to request your association to quickly telegraph the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to forward a telegram to the Chinese ambassador to the United States or directly to the US government to protest and urge them to abolish the new regulations and follow the previous practices. At the very least, they must agree to relax the acidity limit so that our egg factory industry can survive. We have checked that the sale of machine-made eggs from our country to Europe and the United States has been a long-standing practice, but US merchants are meticulously planning to undermine our industry. They first proposed to increase taxes to resist our products, and now they have revised new regulations, limiting the acidity of egg yolk to only five degrees, and rejecting imports if the limit is exceeded. Such excessive restrictions are intended to make Chinese egg yolk disappear. We must understand that the acidity of egg yolk is originally below this limit, but it exceeds this limit due to the time required for waiting for sales. This is a normal physical phenomenon. To rashly consider it spoiled and reject transportation would be tantamount to making our egg yolk unsalable from now on. With the intention of undermining our industry, we should fight for our rights based on reason to maintain our national industry. It is appropriate to telegraph your ministry to review and quickly forward it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to request that it negotiate and stop the excessive limitations of the new regulations and follow the previous practices to maintain the egg industry for the public good. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Notice from the Municipal Organization Department

The Organization Department of the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang yesterday issued a notice to the party headquarters and directly affiliated branches in each district of this city: In order to reorganize the roster of party members throughout the city for easy reference, the Registration Section of the 18th Department Affairs Meeting proposed to recompile the roster of party members in each district of the city. Central Bank Inspection Report

The Central Bank issued its 69th Inspection Report on Issuance Reserves, stating: In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible notes of this bank. The 69th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on October 20, 19th year of the Republic. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: The total amount of convertible notes issued is 22,493,592 silver dollars, including 21,535,892 silver dollar notes and 957,700 auxiliary currency notes. The total amount of reserve fund for convertible notes is 22,493,592 silver dollars, including 20,015,192 silver dollars in cash reserve. The cash reserve is stored in the issuance vault of this bank at 15,590,942.27 silver dollars, in the branches of this bank in various ports at 1,233,797 silver dollars, and in peer banks at 3,190,452.73 silver dollars. The security reserve is equivalent to 2,478,400 silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the security reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the security is less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby made. October 20, 19th year of the Republic. Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank: Li Fuxun. Supervisors: Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, An Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Ji.

Still More Local News Transferred to Later Personnel

Page 15

Local News Two

Bandit Shot Dead on Datong Road Last Night

Thieves Committed Robbery on North Chengdu Road

One Thief Carrying Loot Fled to Datong Road

Discovered by Detectives Who Opened Fire in Pursuit

Thief Shot and Immediately Died

At around 6:20 PM last night, a bandit was shot dead near Siwenli on Datong Road. This bandit had committed a robbery with accomplices at 1472 North Chengdu Road ten minutes before his death. Carrying the loot, he escaped on a No. 3 tram. He got off the tram at the Datong Road intersection and was spotted by detectives from the Xinzha Patrol Station, who stepped forward to search him. The bandit opened fire to resist arrest and was shot and killed on the spot. Both sides fired about twenty shots in total.

The robbery occurred at 1472 North Chengdu Road at around 6:10 PM last night. Three thieves, armed with weapons and speaking with a Shaoxing accent, broke into the house. The victim was unable to resist and was robbed of 98 yuan in cash and silver. The thieves escaped without a trace. The victim reported the incident to the patrol station for investigation. About ten minutes after the incident, Detective No. 275 and Chinese Constable No. 2525 from the Xinzha Patrol Station spotted a man wearing a blue cloth shirt and pants getting off a No. 3 tram on Datong Road in Xinzha. Suspecting his appearance, they decided that he was not a good person. The detectives ordered him to stop and stepped forward to search him.

Bandit Shot Dead. The man, seeing the detectives approaching, panicked and tried to flee north towards Datong Road. He took out a pistol from his pocket and fired two shots at the police. Detective No. 275 and Chinese Constable No. 2525 immediately returned fire. The bandit could not withstand the attack and fled to near Siwenli. He was hit in a vital spot by a bullet and immediately fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. He died soon after. At the time, gunshots cracked and bullets flew, alarming the customers at the nearby Ruyiguan and Xinxingguan restaurants. After the gunshots stopped, passersby gathered around and saw that the dead bandit was about 27 or 28 years old. The bandit's pistol fell to the ground after he was shot. The police collected the pistol, and the body was taken away by the Xinzha Patrol Station's vehicle. The victim of the robbery identified the deceased as one of the bandits who committed the robbery. He still had some of the stolen silver in his pocket, which he had not used.

Accused of Bigamy, Zhang Nai Appeared in Court Yesterday

The Debate Between Both Sides Concluded

Sentencing Scheduled for the Afternoon of the 28th

Zhang Nai, accompanied by his lawyer, arrived in court yesterday. Zhang Nai, a technician at the Wuzhou Guben Soap Factory, was sued by his legal wife, You Yaha, along with Yang Xuejiu, principal of a school in the east of the city, Gong Yu, Yu Yang, and others, for bigamy. After several summonses by the Special District Court, Zhang Nai had failed to appear. Only yesterday, Zhang arrived in court with his lawyer, Chen Tingrui. The other defendants, Yang Xuejiu, Yang's mother Yang Zhou, Zhang's sister Gong Yu, and Zhang's mother Yu Zhang, also appeared in court to be questioned.

Because he inherited two family lines, he had two surnames. In court, he was first asked if Zhang Nai had another surname, and he answered yes. Both Yu and Zhang were his surnames, with Zhang being the inherited line. Previously, he lived in Shanghai and had just returned from Japan and was currently unemployed. His mother, Yu Zhang, was in Hangzhou. You Yaha has been his wife for seventeen years. Yang Xuejiu was married as part of the inherited line, with the wedding taking place on May 24th of this year. This matter was his father's dying wish. While his mother was pregnant with him, he was adopted by his maternal aunt. His aunt had no children and remained a widow, so he inherited her family line, thus becoming a Zhang. His brother, Yu Baoyuan, was also adopted by his paternal uncle.

I approve of the one-man, one-wife system. I cannot inherit the Zhang family line and cut off my family's ancestral line. Therefore, my father always wanted me to take a second wife. I personally did not approve. Although I wanted to practice one-man, one-wife with You, You was not virtuous, so I had to marry Yang. Therefore, I am responsible for the smaller issue, and You is responsible for the larger one. I previously told You to take care of herself, that I would never marry another woman, but You often showed signs of disgust and tried to make me suffer, so I married Yang.

Yaha could have prevented the marriage but did not. At the time, she knew about it. She could have prevented the marriage but did not. At the same time, she went out while I was busy working at the factory. All the trivial matters at home were expected of me, which made me feel very distressed. On March 11th, You left without saying a word. Later, I summoned her to return, but it was unsuccessful. You said that a wife is an outsider, so I had no one else to help me and had to find a way out, so I married Yang.

I once deceived Yang by saying that I had divorced You. I initially told Yang that I was divorced from You. Yang felt very sorry for me and was willing to be my lifelong companion. She had this intention before, but because I was already married, she did not reveal it. As for the things at my residence at 19 Zhiching Lane, Xujiahui, I ordered people to move them to Gong Yu's place. She treated me and You Yaha very well. She usually received a lot of help from me. Instead of appreciating her assistance, I accused her of theft, which I deeply regret. The wedding with Ms. Yang Xuejiu was held at Moore Memorial Church. My mother did not attend the wedding, and so on.

Yang's mother testified that she did not receive the express letter. Yang Zhou testified that she was unable to attend the wedding due to illness. After Zhang and Yang got married, they wanted to go to Japan, so they invited me to the photo studio for a group photo. The court asked if she had received an express letter from You Yaha on December 2nd of last year, to which she replied that she had not. Because at that time, I went to Beijing for school affairs to see Ye Chucang. I returned after seven days, and the letter was not seen.

A wedding at a hotel is not very solemn. Judge Cheng Shangfeng also summoned Pastor Yu Zhizhai of Moore Memorial Church as a witness, who testified that he was 55 years old and officiated the wedding. First, Zhang Nai came to me under the name of Yu Xuelou. I asked what the matter was. Zhang wanted to rent my place for the wedding. He said that he was a university graduate who had studied in the United States and was going to marry Ms. Yang Xuejiu, the principal of a school in the east of the city. Yang's sister was a student at Moore Memorial Church School. I asked why they did not get married at a hotel, implying that I was reluctant. Zhang said that a wedding at a hotel does not have the solemnity of a church. I agreed.

The couple did not commit any crime. When the wedding ceremony was about to begin, I said to the two hundred or so guests, "Ladies and gentlemen, the bride and groom are about to get married. If any of you know of any illegal acts committed by this couple, please speak up." Then I asked the bride and groom the same question, but they did not say anything. I knew that they had not committed any crime. Then I left, and I don't know what happened after that. What I have said is the truth.

Some days after the wedding, Zhang suddenly became unhappy. You Yaha testified that there were still a few simple things to say. Zhang Nai said that he inherited two family lines, but it was actually the Yu family line. He never mentioned before the wedding that he had been instructed to take a second wife. Before the wedding, Zhang also told me that he had no other girlfriends. Some days after the wedding, Zhang went out and returned looking depressed. I asked him, and Zhang replied that a friend had told him that he looked thin and seemed to be sick. I asked who the friend was, and Zhang replied Yang Xuejiu. However, at that time, our relationship was still good. Later, when my aunt arrived, there was a disagreement.

Zhang Nai is Napoleon II. On June 25th, Zhang wanted to throw his son into the Huangpu River, but I stopped him. That's when it ended. On July 23rd, Zhang came home from outside carrying a stone statue of Napoleon. He said that I was Napoleon II. After thinking about it again and again, I realized that Napoleon had divorced his first wife and married another woman. I told Zhang not to become Napoleon. Last November, Zhang attended the World Engineering Conference in Japan. When Zhang went to Japan, Yang Xuejiu personally went to the Huishan Wharf to see him off and gave him gifts.

Chen Tingrui requested an adjournment for reconciliation. The court, seeing that all the testimonies had been completed, ordered the commencement of arguments. Lawyer Chen Tingrui rose to say that he was requesting an adjournment for several days so that there could be room for reconciliation. Lawyer Li Zuyu, representing You Yaha, stated that if the defendant was willing to reconcile, they would not object, or if the court felt that the facts were clear and wanted to proceed with the arguments, they would also express their sympathy. Lawyer Jiang Yiping then said that Yang Xuejiu was in the most unfortunate position, and her suffering was shared by both Zhang and You. According to Yang's personal wishes, the trial should proceed, but for the sake of the entire case, it might be advisable to grant an adjournment to give Zhang and You a chance to reconcile so that there would be no flaws in the future and the families could be reunited, which would be somewhat comforting to Yang.

The debate between both sides was declared concluded. Judge Cheng, seeing that both sides had been delaying until now and had not reconciled, decided to begin the arguments. Then the plaintiff's lawyer, Yang Zuyu, and the defendants' lawyers, Chen Tingrui and Jiang Yiping, debated with each other. The court ordered the conclusion of the debate. Zhang Nai paid a bail of five thousand yuan, and Yang paid a bail to appear when summoned. The others still paid the original bail. The date was changed to the afternoon of the 28th of this month (next Tuesday) at 3:00 PM for sentencing.

Russian Dancer Shot Three Times

The Murderer Surrendered Himself to the Detective

Out of Hatred Because the Woman Loved Another

Astravalva, a Russian dancer aged nineteen, was intimately involved with George Ninya, named Batelizi. Batelizi is currently employed as a bodyguard for a Chinese person, formerly a wealthy merchant who once opened a dance hall in Harbin. At 6:15 PM on the 20th, the two met at a restaurant at 632 Avenue Joffre. After a few words, Batelizi drew a gun and shot the woman. The crowd heard the sound and went to rescue her. Batelizi fired another shot to stop them. Then, he fired three more shots, hitting the woman twice in the left leg and twice in the right leg. The Russian woman fell to the ground in a pool of blood, crying for help. At that time, a French detective happened to be passing by the door. Batelizi surrendered himself and handed over two guns, one of which was a Browning pistol with two bullets remaining. The Russian woman was sent to the hospital, where doctors used X-rays to find that the leg bones had been shattered, and she would no longer be able to work as a dancer even if she recovered in the future. According to Batelizi's confession at the police station, he had been living with the woman for several years. Recently, because he was poor, the woman fell in love with another man, so he angrily did this. It is said that the police station will send Batelizi to the French Concession Court in the coming days to be charged with murder.

Cardsharps Imprisoned

Wei Xiaohua's Wife Cried Loudly in Court

Saying That Her Eighty-Year-Old Mother Had No Means of Living

The master swindlers Wang Xianting, Huang Lushen, Pan Guozhong, Li Song, Wei Xiaohua, Xu Jinsheng, and others, who repeatedly used intimidation and fraud to open rooms in major hotels to set up gambling dens to swindle thousands of dollars from Xie Xiaxun, a famous chess player from Pingyang, and others, were arrested by Bao Detective Liang Chengyu of the Old North Gate Police Station one after another. About 25,000 yuan in ghost money and Eastern Province exchange certificates were seized and sent to the Special District Local Court. Attorney Ru Baoyi of the police station filed a public prosecution, and Xu Jinsheng also hired attorney Jiang Yiping to defend him. The case has been investigated and concluded by Judge Xu, and a date has been set for sentencing. Yesterday morning, the date of the judgment arrived. Judge Xu Jiashi of the Criminal Court came to Criminal Court No. 1 to announce the judgment. The main text stated that Wang Xianting committed five crimes of habitual fraud to obtain property, each crime punishable by three years of imprisonment, a fine of one thousand yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for eight years. One crime of attempted habitual fraud to obtain property was punishable by one year of imprisonment, a fine of five hundred yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for five years. The sentence was six years of imprisonment, a fine of two thousand yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for eight years. Huang Lushen committed four crimes of habitual fraud to obtain property, each crime punishable by three years of imprisonment, a fine of one thousand yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for eight years. One crime of attempted habitual fraud to obtain property was punishable by one year of imprisonment, a fine of five hundred yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for five years. The sentence was five years and six months of imprisonment, a fine of two thousand yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for eight years. Pan Guozhong committed two crimes of habitual fraud to obtain property, each crime punishable by three years of imprisonment, a fine of one thousand yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for eight years. One crime of attempted habitual fraud to obtain property was punishable by one year of imprisonment, a fine of five hundred yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for five years. The sentence was four years and six months of imprisonment, a fine of two thousand yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for eight years. Li Song committed one crime of attempted habitual fraud to obtain property, punishable by one year of imprisonment, a fine of five hundred yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for five years. Wei Xiaohua committed one crime of habitual fraud to obtain property, punishable by three years of imprisonment, a fine of one thousand five hundred yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for eight years. The number of days of detention before the judgment was determined shall be offset by one day of imprisonment for every two days. If the fine is commuted to imprisonment, it shall be offset by one day for every two yuan, but the number of days of imprisonment shall be limited to one year. Xu Jinsheng was found not guilty. The forty-eight ghost money and eleven Eastern Province exchange certificates were confiscated. After the judgment was announced, the defendants were taken away by the police to be executed separately. At that time, Ji, the wife of the defendant Wei Xiaohua, cried and made a fuss in the court. Judge Xu ordered bailiff Fei Congsheng to bring the woman to the court. Attorney Li Zhishan of the police station requested a ruling. Judge Xu asked the woman why she was making a noise in the court. According to her statement, her eighty-year-old mother relied on her husband for a living. Now that her husband was convicted and imprisoned, she felt extremely distressed, so she cried bitterly. Fan Gang, the agent of Wei Xiaohua, immediately requested the court to consider that the woman was ignorant and to leniently order her to return. Judge Xu declared to Ji that if she disagreed with the judgment, she could appeal according to the law and could not make unreasonable noise in the court. She should be punished, but considering her ignorance and that it was her first offense, she was ordered to return and not repeat such behavior. Ji agreed and left.

The Tragic Death of Xin Dingchang

The French Police Station Sent Detectives to Investigate

The Body Was Examined Yesterday

Xin Dingchang, a sampan man, was shot into the river by a French sailor for no reason on the evening of the 16th of this month, and tragically drowned. The details were published in the 18th issue of this newspaper. It is now learned that the body of the deceased has already floated up, but all sectors have been outraged by this incident. The Party Headquarters has also issued a declaration to the people of the country. The details of the case are as follows:

The truth of the incident is that Xin was thirty years old and from Ningbo. Since childhood, he learned rowing skills on the No. 110 sampan rowed by his father, Hesheng. Later, when he grew older and had considerable physical strength, his father bought a new sampan, registered as No. 130, and ordered his son to row it. Xin operated at the Widetoma Road pier in Yangshupu. On the evening of the 16th of this month, two sailors from the French Waldeck-Rousseau warship, which was docked in the Huangpu River, hired Xin's sampan to cross to the French cannon sand merchant ship (transliteration) docked in the center of the river to visit friends. They did not pay the fare and boarded the ship, asking Xin to wait for a while, as they still wanted to return to shore. After a long time, three sailors from the ship took Ge A Mao's chartered sampan ashore, and the two sailors also followed down, crossing Xin's sampan to Ge's sampan, intending to evade Xin's fare. Xin saw that the situation was not good and stopped the sailor in the back to ask for money. The sailor was unreasonable and started punching and kicking him on the spot. Xin did not expect that he would suddenly attack and was not prepared, so he was knocked into the river and drowned. This is the truth of what happened when the tragedy occurred. After the French soldier caused the accident, he did not try to rescue him and instead took another sampan and forcibly tried to go ashore. The sampan man was also unhappy with his unprovoked killing of people, so he gathered the neighboring boats to try to stop the soldier and hand him over to the water patrol police station for investigation. Seeing that the situation was not good, the soldier snatched the road ashore and disappeared without a trace.

The police station investigated the matter and the deceased's father, Hesheng, learned that his son had died tragically, so he cried to the water patrol police station. Police chief Kaili reported the case and ordered West Detective Pang Shihua and Detective Deng Jiagen to board the ship for investigation. At the same time, Ge A Mao and Zhu Gensheng, two sampan men from No. 1156 and No. 795, also went to the police station and were willing to testify. The next day (17th) at 10:00 AM, Police Chief Pang of the police station and Detective Deng went to the French Consulate to meet with the French Deputy Consul to report the case. The Consul said that the case was related to the navy and asked Pang to visit the Chief Patrol Officer of the French Police Station. After mutual consultation, the police station sent one Chinese and one Western detective each to accompany Pang Deng back to the French ship for investigation at 2:00 PM. On the spot, they found three original sailors who had boarded the ship before and after the French soldier. The three sailors also confessed that they had witnessed the French soldier hitting Xin into the river. However, they did not pay attention to the appearance of the French soldier because it was too sudden, so they had forgotten. The detectives returned to the police station to report that they had not obtained any key information.

The attitude of the French Consulate was that on the morning of the 18th, the detectives visited the French Deputy Consul for the second time and requested that they be allowed to board the warship to investigate and identify the soldiers who caused the accident. The Consul said that he had to obtain the consent of the captain of the warship first and agreed to contact him on his behalf. At 1:00 PM, the water patrol police station suddenly received a phone call from the French Police Station saying that the French Consul had discussed the matter with the warship, but the captain said that he refused to allow them to board the ship. Because the murderer had not been found, the head of the water patrol police station believed that the case was difficult to solve, so he ordered detectives to go to the French Consulate to discuss the matter on the 20th. The French Consul said that the customs could propose to proceed with diplomatic procedures.

The court examined the body. Xin drowned and his body floated to the surface of the river near Yangshupu the day before yesterday. The Chinese police of the water patrol police station recovered the body and took it to the police station. They then notified Hesheng, the father of the deceased, to come to the scene to identify the body. Hesheng could not help but cry when he saw the body of his son. The head of the police station ordered the body to be handed over to the patrol boat of the Lifeboat Bureau to be transported to the Bureau's mortuary. Deng Jiagen was dispatched to submit a report to the local court, requesting an autopsy. Yesterday afternoon, the prosecutor appointed by the court came to the Bureau to examine the body and ordered the body to be received and buried by the father of the deceased after signing a guarantee, pending verification.

Hometown assistance: The Ningbo Association in Shanghai, after investigating the case of Xin Dingchang, a fellow villager who was brutally shot into the river and killed by a French sailor, dispatched personnel to investigate and confirmed that the facts were true. It immediately convened an emergency meeting to discuss methods of assistance and decided to send a letter to the French Concession Court requesting a fair and thorough investigation, strict punishment of the murderers, and demanding compensation for the loss.

News After Liu Junfu Was Accused

Qiao Jiyuan, Member of the Party Standing Committee

Was Suddenly Accused of False Accusation by Liu

Liu Junfu of Huajing Town, a southwest village in Shanghai, was previously accused by Chen Xinlou of being a local tyrant and evil gentry. At that time, the local merchants and people submitted a public report to the county government, and the Sixth Branch of the Second District of the Shanghai County Party Department also reported Liu. The Second District Party Department submitted it to the Shanghai County Party Department, which appointed Comrade Lü Juefei to investigate and confirm the case. The Shanghai Local Court investigated the case of Chen's accusation against Liu for three or four weeks. Three or four weeks ago, it was suddenly reported that the court had dismissed the case against Liu Junfu. However, the plaintiff, Chen Xinlou, had not received the dismissal order for some reason. According to the Criminal Procedure Law, the dismissal order must be delivered to the informant and the defendant within seven days after the dismissal. If there is any objection, they may apply for reconsideration. The plaintiff is thoroughly investigating the overdue dismissal order. Unexpectedly, Liu Junfu suddenly used lightning speed to sue Chen Xinlou, Qiao Jiyuan, and others for false accusations in the Shanghai Local Court. Qiao is a member of the Standing Committee of the Sixth Branch of the Second District Party Department. He has now hired lawyer Zhou Xiaoan to handle the litigation. The general idea of his defense is: (1) When Chen Xinlou accused Liu Junfu of being a local tyrant, Qiao was neither a co-plaintiff nor had any relationship with him, so he did not constitute a reason for false accusation; (2) The report of the Sixth Branch of the Second District of the Shanghai County Party Department against Liu for being a local tyrant was submitted by the Branch to the Second District Party Department and then to the Shanghai County Party Department. The County Party Department appointed Comrade Lü Juefei to investigate and confirm the case. At that time, Qiao Jiyuan was only a member of the Standing Committee of the Sixth Branch. According to the regulations, all matters of the Branch must be decided by the majority of the Executive Committee and handled by the Executive Committee in accordance with the resolutions. Therefore, the report of the local tyrant was purely an action of the entire Party Department and was not Qiao Jiyuan's personal action. This time, the plaintiff not only made a mistake in the subject of the litigation, but also had no reason for the allegations. The case is scheduled to be heard today (22nd) at 3:00 PM. Qiao went to the County Party Department yesterday to report everything. The County Party Department, seeing that Liu Junfu had resumed his old ways shortly after his report, did not understand the difference between public legal persons and private legal persons and intended to harm him. Therefore, it intended to provide assistance to Qiao Jiyuan and others based on the old case.

Lin Long Dies by Poisoning

On the 18th of this month, a man from Fujian named Lin Long arrived at Room 439 of the Central Hotel on Wuma Road, Hubei Road, and told the tea server to wake him up the next morning. The tea server agreed. The next morning, the tea server went to the room but found the door tightly closed. After knocking without a response, the tea server suspected something was wrong and broke the door open. Lin was lying on the bed, his face pale and lifeless. He appeared to have taken opium poison. The tea server reported to the front desk, who in turn reported to the Lao Zha Police Station in charge of the area. Detectives were ordered to take the body to the mortuary on Fietou Road for examination. Yesterday morning, Xu Mei, a prosecutor from the Special District District Court, arrived at the mortuary to confirm the cause of death. As no family members were found, it was ordered that the body be taken to the Pushan Villa for burial.

Compensation Issues in the Tragic Death of Xia Axin

Demanding a Loss of 15,000 Taels

Xia Axin, a 55-year-old Ningbo man residing at No. 37, Shan Zhong Road, in the French Concession and working as a launderer, was riding a bicycle in front of his door at 3 PM on the 3rd of this month, intending to go somewhere. A cargo truck driven by Wang Xingchang and a car driven by Mao Youlun were approaching from both directions, causing Xia to be unable to avoid them and being struck and killed by Wang's truck. Details of the incident were previously reported. Yesterday, the police brought all the witnesses to the French Court for investigation. The plaintiff, the deceased's wife Xia Liangshi, complained that her husband had been tragically struck and killed, requesting justice. Attorney Ted Beck, representing the plaintiff, stated that the deceased had just left his house and was about to get on his bicycle when he was struck by Wang Xingchang's truck. The location where he was struck was a place where cars should not have been driving, indicating that the deceased was not at fault. The blame should be borne by both defendants. The deceased left behind a wife and young children, all of whom relied on him for support. Now that he has been struck and killed, they have no one to rely on. Therefore, they are requesting compensation for a loss of 15,000 taels. Defendant Mao Youlun, represented by Attorney Ba He, argued that two issues need to be studied in this case. The first is the issue of responsibility, which requires proving which of the two defendants was at fault. My client's car was traveling from north to south and saw a person on a bicycle ahead. To avoid danger, he immediately swerved to the left. Unexpectedly, Wang Xingchang's truck came speeding from the opposite direction, first overturning my client's car and then striking the deceased. From this perspective, the responsibility should be borne by the second defendant, Wang Xingchang. The second is the issue of loss. In the case of Shen Pengnian, who was struck and killed, my law firm previously represented the family. Mr. Shen was highly respected in the literary world and earned six to seven hundred yuan a month. He had many children at home. At that time, they demanded a loss of 20,000 yuan, but the court only awarded 6,000 yuan in compensation. The loss demanded by the plaintiff in this case is far too large. At this point, it was past noon, and the Chinese and Western officials adjourned to await further hearing and verification.

Coal Pile Suddenly Ignites Due to Carelessness

At around 5 AM yesterday morning, dozens of tons of loose coal piled up in the wasteland of the Third Coal Depot of Mitsui Yoko, across from the Huishan Wharf in Pudong. Due to a worker's carelessness, a cigarette butt was thrown into the loose coal, causing it to suddenly ignite, with thick smoke billowing and flames raging. The Yangshupu Fire Brigade dispatched a fire boat to douse the flames, which were extinguished after a short while. Only a few tons of loose coal were burned, and fortunately, the fire did not spread to the foundations of the warehouses.

Young Woman Sues Husband for Assault and Expulsion, Seeking Divorce

Cai Linzhen (i.e., Zhu Cai's wife), a young woman from this locality, recently engaged a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the District Court against her husband, Zhu Qiuyan, for divorce. Her grounds are repeated abuse and expulsion, as well as the removal and concealment of her dowry. Her objectives are divorce, the return of her dowry valued at 1,277 yuan, and alimony (i.e., support payments) of 700 yuan. Her statement roughly states that the plaintiff is 19 years old, resides at 161 Xin Puyu Road, and was married to the defendant, Zhu Qiuyan, through a matchmaker on December 12th of last year. In January of the following year, the defendant ordered the plaintiff to return to her mother's home to borrow 200 yuan. Before long, the defendant again ordered the plaintiff to borrow money. Because the plaintiff had nowhere to borrow from, she politely refused. The defendant resented this and beat the plaintiff, while removing and concealing her dowry at Zhang Tinggui's home (Zhang is the defendant's foster father), and so on. At the previous hearing, the defendant Zhu Qiuyan did not appear. His mother, Zhu Wu, appeared in court and argued that her son and daughter-in-law had a good relationship and that he had not beaten her, only had verbal arguments. The court ordered a re-summons. Yesterday, the hearing continued. At 10 AM, Judge Zhang Jinjian again opened the second courtroom. Both parties arrived with their lawyers, and there were many spectators, mostly women who were relatives of the defendant. After the judge took the bench, he ordered the defendant, Zhu Qiuyan, to the stand. He stated that he was 18 years old, a local resident, and lived at 28 Tianzhutang Street, south of Malu Bridge. He currently works as a typesetter in the printing house in North Nicheng Bridge and is still learning his trade. The plaintiff is his legal wife. Because she often returns to Ningbo, they sometimes have verbal arguments, but he has not beaten her. (Question) Did you order the plaintiff to borrow money? (Answer) No. (Question) Is the house you live in your own property? (Answer) Yes. (Question) Are you currently trying to sell it? (Answer) Yes, but we haven't agreed on a price yet. (Question) Where is the plaintiff's dowry now? (Answer) Still at home. (Question) What is your opinion on the plaintiff's request for divorce? (Answer) I don't want it. (Question) Did you beat her on June 2nd and June 22nd of this year? (Answer) No. The judge, having obtained the testimony, ordered the plaintiff, Cai Linzhen, to the stand and attempted to reconcile them, advising the plaintiff not to divorce and to return to good terms. (Answer) He doesn't want me outside. It's not that easy now. As for saying that I returned to my mother's home, ask yourself, if my mother is sick, shouldn't I go home to visit her? Next, witness Zhang Tinggui testified that he was 52 years old and lived across from the Dafochang. Zhu Qiuyan is my foster son. The court ordered him to provide a written testimony to be kept on file. (Question) Are the two of them on good terms? (Answer) I heard they were. (Question) Do you know about Qiuyan borrowing money? (Answer) No. (Question) Did he sell the house? (Answer) Yes, but it hasn't been resolved yet. (Question) Is the plaintiff's dowry kept at your house? (Answer) No, that's not the case. (Question) Did you try to mediate? (Answer) Yes, I did. The plaintiff's mother escorted the plaintiff to the defendant's house. The two families had a dispute. I tried to mediate once, but I don't know about other matters. Another witness, a woman named Xing Shen, testified that she was 60 years old and lived on Meixie Road. She was indeed the matchmaker. At first, she heard that they were getting along well, but she doesn't know how they started arguing later. The judge then invited Prosecutor Wu to the court to express his opinion and declared the debate open. The lawyers for both parties stood up and debated back and forth. The plaintiff's side requested that a divorce be granted, as well as compensation for alimony of 700 yuan and the return of her dowry valued at 1,277 yuan. The defendant's lawyer stated that if the plaintiff insisted on a divorce, she must compensate for the loss of 1,455.9 yuan from the wedding. The judge then declared the debate closed and set the judgment for the 25th of this month. Thereupon, the court adjourned.

Pirate Attack on Pinghu Ferry

Merchants Suffer Significant Losses

In the counties under the jurisdiction of Pudong and West Shanghai, more cotton is planted than rice. Now is the time when cotton from various villages is coming onto the market. Various flower merchants and flower shops in Shanghai have sent their staff to the villages with cash to buy small amounts of cotton in order to make a small profit. There are many such people. However, the atmosphere of bandits in the countryside is not peaceful, and merchants are often robbed on the way, especially in the towns and villages at the intersection of Songjiang and Shanghai. The other day, Chen Kaitai and Lu Hongtai flower shops each sent their staff with more than 3,000 yuan in cash to the villages to buy flowers, accompanied by flower merchant Zhou Jiankang (Zhou also carried more than 1,800 yuan). They boarded the Pinghu regular ferry to various villages to buy flowers. When the ferry arrived at Jin Siliang Bridge in Shanghai City at midnight, it was suddenly encountered by a pirate ship. Five bandits, each holding a box cannon and a pistol, jumped onto the ferry and ransacked the passengers, leaving no one spared. All the cash carried by the flower merchants, Zhou Jiankang and others, totaling more than 5,000 yuan, was robbed. The robbers obtained their loot, abandoned the boat, and escaped ashore. Zhou and others have now returned to Shanghai to report to the owners of the shops and report to the relevant authorities to request an arrest.

Laborer Killed by Car

Driver Fined 40 Yuan

Plus 600 Yuan in Compensation

Zhang Taicheng, father of Jiangbei woman Huang Zhangshi, was working as a road laborer when he was struck and killed on the 19th of last month on the Bund of the French Concession by a truck driven by driver Yu Amao. The incident was reported to the French Court, and Judge Zhu conducted an on-site examination and ordered the body to be collected. The police summoned the defendant to the French Court for questioning and awaited a decision. Yesterday, the judgment was reached. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced the defendant Yu Amao to a fine of 40 yuan and ordered him to pay the deceased's family 600 yuan in compensation as a warning.

Wang Hanlun Cigarettes

Without Consent of the Individual

Wang Sues for Compensation

Film star Wang Hanlun, represented by a lawyer, filed a lawsuit in the French Court, stating that the defendant, Datongnan Tobacco Company, has been manufacturing Wang Hanlun brand cigarettes and selling them in the north since 1928. Her lawyer previously sent a letter to the Hebei Tobacco Tax Bureau, which replied with a letter proving that the defendant's company was producing the cigarettes. The letter is now presented for review. The defendant's company manufactured these brand cigarettes without the plaintiff's prior consent, which is inappropriate. The plaintiff is requesting three things: (1) Confiscation of the cigarettes that have not yet been sold. (2) Prohibition of further manufacturing. (3) Compensation for losses based on business standards. Please investigate the number of products. Calculate each box at 10 yuan, for a total reputation loss of 30,000 yuan. The defendant was also represented by a lawyer, who argued that the plaintiff's allegations were not true. These cigarettes were actually produced by a certain tobacco company, which sold them to a certain factory, which then resold them to the defendant as a gift. The plaintiff should sue the manufacturer, as it has nothing to do with the defendant. Please investigate clearly. The judge adjourned the hearing for further review.

Interrogation of Robbers in the Zhaofeng Road Robbery Case

Mao Xiaomao, a Chongming native, worked as a rickshaw puller and lived at No. 570 Zhaofeng Road. At around 1 AM on the 9th of this month, robbers broke into his home and used weapons to rob him of silver and jewelry worth 1,530 yuan. He reported the incident to the Harbin Police Station. Detectives Yan Shiqing, Zhou Kaiwen, Liu Decheng, and others arrested Shen Zhixiang, a Haaimen native, the ringleader of the robbery, in Room 4 of the Kenenghai Road Hu-Ning Hotel. Shen had previously pulled a rickshaw for Mao Xiaomao. The defendant was handed over to the Special District Court for interrogation and detention. This newspaper reported the details. The other day, the Chinese and Western detectives in charge of the case learned that there were still accomplices hiding at No. 2186 Disiwei Road and No. 33 Jiaotong Road. They secretly went to these locations and arrested Zhang Linlin, Liang Lishi, and Zhang Liantao, all from Tongzhou, and brought them into the police station. Yesterday morning, they were brought to the Third Criminal Court of the Special Court along with Shen Zhixiang. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, presented the case. The victim, Mao Xiaomao, stated that a total of five robbers came that night and robbed him of 630 yuan in cash, 520 yuan in paper money, 200 dimes, a gold bracelet, eight gold rings, a gold band, four gold buttons, and two watches. The silver was the money he had collected during the day. He witnessed the defendant Liang Lishi opening the box and robbing it. He did not see the other robbers. Witness Gong Xishan testified that Zhang Linlin held a gun and threatened him, but he did not see the others. Shen Mao's wife testified that Xiaomao was her father. That night, the defendant Zhang Liantao took off two gold rings from her finger and robbed her of a watch. However, Shen Zhixiang was out that morning and did not return. Child Lu Kaolang testified that the defendant Liang Lishi was present at the scene. Shen Zhixiang then stated that he was the one who initiated the case and first notified Zhang Linlin, who then invited six people to rob. He did not go himself. He received 75 yuan afterward. Zhang Linlin confessed that although Shen invited him, he did not go either. He received 45 yuan afterward. Liang Lishi confessed that he was invited by Shen on the pretext of going out to play. He went to the plaintiff's door and took out a gun, telling him to stand guard outside. He received 24 yuan afterward. Shen and a friend of his, along with Zhang Liantao, went inside to rob. Zhang Liantao confessed that he stood guard inside the door and then fled. He received 24 yuan afterward. Judge Ge Zhitan verified the testimonies and ordered the four defendants, Zhang Linlin and others, to be taken back into custody to await further questioning.

China Merchants and Two Other Companies Negotiate Rules for Managing Tea Servers on the Shanghai-Ningbo Route

The Shanghai Shipping Association previously received instructions from the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs that the tea servers on the Shanghai-Ningbo route ships operated by China Merchants, Sanbei, and Ning-Shao were extorting tips from passengers, causing travelers great hardship. The association was instructed to find a way to stop this. After receiving the order, the association convened a meeting of the above companies and reported the results to the Bureau of Social Affairs. The other day, the Bureau of Social Affairs sent Mr. Zhang Zhenyuan to the Shipping Association to request that the companies concerned be convened again to formulate unified rules for managing tea servers in order to restrict them. Yesterday, the China Merchants and two other companies were convened at the association to discuss the matter. As a result of the meeting, a draft of these management regulations was made and will be sent to the general manager's office of each company for review before being sent to the Shipping Association and forwarded to the Bureau of Social Affairs for consideration and implementation.

Record of the Autumn General Meeting of the Physicians' Association

The Shanghai Physicians' Association held its autumn general meeting at Yipinxiang at 7 PM on the 19th. More than 80 members attended, including Xu Naili, Wang Qizhang, Xu Yimin, Zhou Junchang, Cheng Hanzhang, Qie Zhenxun, Song Guobin, and Zhu Qiluo. The Municipal Party Department sent Mao Yun to attend and provide guidance. The meeting was conducted in accordance with etiquette. Chairman Xu Naili reported on the cases handled by the spring general meeting and the general situation of the association's affairs since June. Economic Committee member Xie Yunshou reported on the income and expenditure accounts. Editor-in-Chief Cheng Hanzhang reported on the editing situation of New Medicine and Society. Fundraising team leaders Zhou Junchang and Ye Nansheng reported on the achievements in raising funds for the National New Medicine and Pharmacy Association. Then, the chairman introduced new members Ma Yinliang, Liu Yixiang, Wang Jingyang, and Wang Yijing to the members. The following motions were then discussed: (1) Cheng Hanzhang proposed that, in the case of lawsuits between patients and members, no reports should be published in the newspapers before a court decision is made in order to maintain the reputation of physicians. The motion was passed, but the words "members" should be changed to "medical community." (2) Wang Qizhang proposed a discussion of the legal issues of the Physicians' Association, explaining that the Western Medicine Regulations passed by the Legislative Yuan are stricter than the Ministry of Health's Provisional Regulations for Physicians, requiring examinations according to foreign standards, and that examinations cannot be held, and registration is naturally not possible. The association and its members no longer have a legal basis. Therefore, he proposed that the association discuss a proper solution. It was decided to hand it over to the Executive Committee, which would appoint a special committee to organize a committee to consider the matter at length. (3) Chen Rongzhang proposed that the association should be responsible for protecting its members in the event of disputes or lawsuits between patients and members. The motion was passed, but it must be divided into two types: (A) Disputes concerning medical treatment and medicine shall be certified or mediated by the association. (B) In the case of lawsuits, the association shall entrust a legal advisor to handle the case for the member concerned. However, the lawyer's fees shall still be borne by the member concerned. (4) Discussion of Article 1 of the association's constitution: The Shanghai Physicians' Association shall be renamed the Shanghai Municipal Physicians' Association. The motion was passed. (5) Discussion of the association's editorial department issue. It was decided to hand it over to the Executive Committee for handling. Then, Mao Yun, a representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave a guiding speech. The chairman gave a response. Then a banquet was held. During the banquet, the staff was re-elected. As a result, Xu Naili, Ye Zhisheng, Song Guobin, Niu Huisheng, Jiang Zhenxun, Chu Minyi, Zhu Qiluo, Zhou Junchang, Wang Zhangfu, Chen Rongzhang, Li Ding, You Pengxi, Wang Yugang, Wu Jishun, and Tang Chou first were elected as executive committee members. Li Chishi, Tu Maolin, Wu Zongqing, Sun Cuicun, and Xi Shitai were elected as alternate executive committee members. Wang Qizhang, Yu Yunxiu, Xia Shenchu, Cai Wanmen, and Pang Jingzhou were elected as supervisory committee members. Cheng Hanzhang and Yu Bin were elected as alternate supervisory committee members. The meeting was adjourned at 11 PM.

Letter Requesting Construction of New-Style Slaughterhouses

Commodity Inspection Bureau Sends Letter to Governments of Various Cities and Counties in Jiangsu and Zhejiang

The livestock products and by-products of our country have always been a major part of export commodities. The annual value of national products is about 200 million yuan. However, in recent years, various countries have used the excuse that the livestock of our country do not meet sanitary standards and have banned imports, causing significant losses to domestic merchants. The reason is that provinces and counties in our country have not established new-style slaughterhouses and cannot provide effective proof that livestock products have undergone pre-slaughter and post-slaughter inspection. The Livestock Products and By-products Inspection Office of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, in view of this, is actively promoting the establishment of public slaughterhouses and implementing pre-slaughter and post-slaughter inspection so that the export products of our country can meet world public health conditions and foreigners can no longer find excuses. Previously, it sent personnel to various places to investigate the situation of slaughterhouses and submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the Ministry of Health and forward it to the provincial and municipal governments to order the governments of cities and counties along the railway to establish new-style slaughterhouses in the city and county centers. Recently, in order to widely promote and promote early realization, it published a small booklet on the reasons and methods for building public slaughterhouses in various provinces, cities, and counties across the country and sent it to the governments of various cities and counties in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, requesting that they find a way to construct new-style slaughterhouses with relatively complete scale in the central areas within one year to meet the needs. It is now reported that the governments of Dongyang and Jiaxing counties in Zhejiang Province have replied that they are planning and preparing to construct them.
